<Author>Spaceman58
<Content>Our best hotel experience in Hawaii Anyone who has been to Honolulu immediately understands what I mean when I say it is crowded and congested, very touristy, offering little in the way of tropical paradise often associated with Hawaii, and with too much traffic. My wife and I have spent some time there and concluded that we never need to spend any more time in this capitol city.One hotel has single-handedly changed our minds about Honolulu, and now we can't wait to return.We spent a couple of weeks on three Hawaiian islands in July 2008. We needed to get back to Honolulu for our last night so we could catch a 7 am flight back to the mainland, so after reviewing numerous accommodations on tripadvisor, I settled on the Outrigger Reef on the Beach (rated #16 at the time I booked). How I wish we had arranged for more than one night in this excellent hotel.First, let me say that, yes, there is major construction going on at this hotel. It was actually a little difficult to find, but once we located it, we were treated like royalty. The staff called us by name throughout our stay, and were courteous and very helpful. I can honestly say I have never encountered such as excellent staff at any hotel. They enthusiastically assisted with every request, and offered several good tips.We received a wonderful room upgrade and abolutely loved our room. Our balcony looked out on Diamond Head and the beach. The bathroom was nicely appointed and very spacious.The bell captain, a young man named Kawika, took us to our room and actually checked us in on our balcony. When I casually mentioned that our anniversary was the next day, he immediately sent up a complimentary bottle of champaign. Kawika, you are the best - thank you!The rooms have recently been updated with nice furnishings and comfortable beds. The rest of the hotel will be brought up to those standards later this year.The pool is beautifully tiled and is sandwiched between two towers, offering shade through much of the day. When we were there, Waikiki Beach was quite rocky directly outside this hotel, but that can change with the tide and the seasons. It might be fine now.The Outrigger had an excellent restaurant and shops inside. It is also extremely close to the US Army Museum of Hawaii, and across the street from Roy's Hawaiian Fusion restaurant, which provided us with our best meal on the islands.I simply cannot say enough positive things about this hotel. And it is the staff that makes it special. Once the construction ends, I expect this to be a top 10 or even top 5 Honolulu hotel on tripadvisor, and it deserves to be that high.We visited Hawaii with friends, who happened to stay at the Moana Surfrider. They were also upgraded to a suite when they checked in, but our room was better than theirs, with a better view. They visited us in our room, helped share our champaign, and were impressed with our accommodations. I can proudly say our experience at the Outrigger was better than theirs at the Surfrider.To the staff at the Outrigger Reef on the Beach, I want to say thank you. You have earned our affection and loyalty. We will return to visit for a longer stay as soon as we can.

Only wished the sun wasn't shaded so early in the day by the buildings.The women working in the gift shop were very helpful and pleasant.The beach services located directly out in front of the Shorebird resturant were fantastic and a great addition to the Hotel. I wish I could remember the names of the other three, two men and one gal, who went out of their way to be sure we had a fun experience. I started out the surfing lesson with an upset stomach and when I actually got sick a long way from shore, I was brought in and so well taken care of. I appreicated it so much! I will stay here again and will recommend it to my friends. Thank you for making our trip such a fun memory!Peggy NielsenSeattle, WA

<Author>gorams
<Content>Great Value, Service and Beach Had a wonderful stay. Our room category was partial ocean view. I have stayed at other hotels with partial ocean views and this one had a great view of the ocean. I was able to get up in the morning and see the surfers from my balcony. The property is on the beach, so needless to say, a short stroll from the elevator and you are on the beach. There are vendors that rent chairs, umbrella's, and water toys. The Shore Bird is a great value for breakfast. I have been to the island several times and they offer a buffet breakfast for $12.95. This is a great value considering some hotels charge up to $32.00 for breakfast. The hotel's pool is open and there is still construction at the property. For the value and location the construction was not a bother to me. Several restaraunts are within walking distance if you don't want to take advantage of the hotel restaraunts. The hotel offers transfers to and from the airport, the aloha stadium - I bought my transfers from a tour operator before hand and was disappointed to see that the hotel offered them at a lower rate, they also have a tour desk. Enjoyed my stay and am looking forward to a return visit.

<Author>flydrive&fun
<Content>Such attention to detail! After spending months reading reviews of the many, many hotels on the Waikiki Beach strip, we decided on the Outrigger Reef on the Beach because of the location right on the beach. We booked an ocean view room through one of the airline travel agencies, kind of hoped for an upgrade to a ocean front room, but the brand new ocean view room we were assigned was absolutely wonderful. We were on the end (1003) so our balcony was quite large. We overlooked the ocean on the right, the koi pond and the pool below, and overlooked other hotel areas and beyond to the left. Our stay included the daily breakfast buffet at the Shorebird - what could be better, a wonderful brunch open air at the beach!The first morning after our arrival we participated in the vow renewal ceremony on the beach that the hotel offers - free of charge. We had pre-arranged this. It was well beyond any expectation that we had! The ceremony was so full of Hawaiian tradition. Everything was explained as we went along, and it was truly a memorable occasion. The hotel allows a freelance photographer to shoot pictures at the ceremony, and your purchase is optional. This is done only as a courtesy - they in no way make you feel obligated. We did purchase the disc he offered, and are very happy with the many, many photos that were taken. Following the early ceremony we had breakfast at the Shorebird. Although it is buffet they do, of course, have table attendants. One of the waitstaff asked us about our number of years together, and he remembered us each morning that we came in. This made us feel so welcome. Everyone on the concierge staff, the valet and bell staff were beyond helpful. The in-room check in process after the long travel was such a welcome surprise. The morning we were ready to drive our rental to Pearl Harbor, the valet gave us tips how to avoid rush hour traffic on the drive. The view of Diamondhead from the beach right outside our hotel was priceless. All in all, the Outrigger Reef on the Beach was the perfect choice!

<Author>eve24
<Content>Loved the Outrigger! We stayed at the Outrigger Reef on the Beach for 4 nights from Oct. 19-23, 2007 for our first trip to Honolulu. We paid for a city view and were upgraded to a partial ocean view. Our room rate of $169 included free daily breakfast and parking(normally $25/day). It was a great deal especially since this hotel is right on Waikiki Beach. The hotel is also close to many shops and restaurants. The newly renovated rooms and balconies were gorgeous! The staff were very friendly and helpful. We enjoyed using the fitness center which had a good selection of equipment and weights. There is a Starbucks and Jamba Juice conveniently located in the lobby. In the basement level, there is a kiosk to print boarding passes for Hawaiian Airlines(HA) which was perfect since we were flying to Kauai via HA from Honolulu. There is also a laundry room for guests on the premises. The breakfast buffet at the Shorebird was good but I did not like the coffee. We enjoyed meals at Roys(across the street), the Yardhouse( 2 blocks away at the Beach Walk) and Duke's Canoe Club (at the Outrigger Waikiki Hotel- a 10 minute walk away). We rented a car for a couple of days and drove to Diamond Head and Pearl Harbor. Overall, we enjoyed our stay in Honolulu and at the Outrigger Reef.

<Content>Quit Your Moaning We went back to the Outrigger Reef for the second year and were a little concerned by some of the reviews we read about construction going on in the area. The good news is that the rooms in the tower that have been renovated are far superior to the old rooms and are extremely well decorated and maintained - a 1000% improvement over the older rooms. yes there is construction going on at the hotel and because of this the lobby is not as nice as it used to be or will be in the future so if you seek perfection do not stay here. All the staff were extremely friendly and helpful and the rooms were cleaned efficiently and before noon every day. the pool is surrounded by some of the construction and I guess my message to folks would be why go the pool in Hawaii? the beach is close by although as many folks have complained, it is a little bit rocky - boo hoo - walk 200 yards and be on the beautiful sandy beach that fronts the royal hawaiin.Both restaurants are still operational, the shorebird is a little bit funky with the cook your own entree but the price is reasonable and it can be fun. the Ocean house is really good and my meal there which was ordered different to the entree on the menu was served exactly as ordered and very quickly by a very personable and efficient server.Overall if you want to avoid a big city feel (trump hotel is going up directly opposite) stay away from Oahu in general - this area has lots of older hotels that quite rightly are being upgraded. If you want the joy of rolling out of bed and stepping into the sand a couple of minutes later - this is a great place - we will certainly be back!

<Rating>4	-1	5	5	4	3	3	3	

<Author>lajollagirl
<Content>Good location but nothing special My husband and I stayed at the Outrigger Reef Dec. 06 for the Honolulu Marathon. The locatiion: Location is the best part abouut the hotel. Walk past the lobby, through the Shore Bird Restaurant, and you're on the beach with gorgeous views of Waikiki Beach and Diamond Head. For the price, it's really not a bad hotel - remember, you're on Waikiki Beach, and most other hotels here will charge $$$ for the same locatiion but better accomodations. Shopping and dining are all within walking distance. If you want to venture out of Waikiki defnitely rent a car. We can only handle so much shopping so opted for this choice to drive to other beaches, sites around the island. Beware however, they charge a steep $18 a day to park and there is no nearby off-site parking. Parking is valet only - no self park, so we felt the need to tip the guys running to get our car for every trip, so parking was more like $20 a day. The staff: No problems with the front desk. The staff didn't treat us like royalty 5 star, but it's not a 5 star hotel - you get what you pay for considering this is Waikiki. Nice enough staff for the hotel rating. I did like the fact that the timeshare people left us alone. There's nothing worse than being harassed by timeshare people the moment you have just arrived to a hotel after a long flight. The pool staff was very poor however. I had asked for a menu from the waitress and she never returned with a menu. Had to get up myself to get the menu. The rooms: We had a partial ocean view. On the plus side, I did like the location of our room b/c it was a corner room on the side opposite Diamond Head. We had a nice view of the park to our right, then a partial ocean view to our left. I wouldn't recommend a room w/o a partial ocean view at least. There's a lot of construction going on daily in Waikiki and don't be surprised if you have a view of construction equipment and extra noise if you go with a 'city' view. Our rooms were cleaned daily, towels replaced etc. early enough for our return to our rooms in the late afternoon to clean up for dinner. I also liked that they have a small refridgerator and safe. On the negative side: The rooms had a bit of a musty/moldy smell to them. Our room was non-smoking, but we could also smell a hint of cigarette smoke. The halls to our room level especially reeked of smoke. The layout of the rooms are very outdated. The bathroom was very very small and had a very odd layout - the closet was actually in the walkway of the bathroom. No bathtub so the shower stall is very small. If you want something with nicer rooms, updated decor, cleaner, more ammenities, for the same price, don't stay in Waikiki. We stayed at Turtle Bay Resort which is on the North Shore - a bit of a drive to the Waikiki, but for the same price, you'll have all the things that a Waikiki 3 1/2 star hotel lacks. The pool: clean for the amount of guests, but we were there in December so it wasn't exactlly scorching hot. It was a bit windy that week so there weren't a lot of people in the pool to begin with. Summer would probably be a different story. The pool staff was unattentive. Pool is definitely outdated. You'll be better off at the beach.The food. There is a starbux on site which was a plus, although we prefer local Hawaiian coffee shops. Interestingly enough, brewed Kona coffee was NO WHERE to be found at most cafes we went to, unlike the other islands. But I was glad starbux was there - consistent and you know what to expect. We only ate at the Shore Bird Restaurant at the hotel which has a nice view of the beach. We had the daily breakfast included with the room charge. If you have to pay extra for the breakfast to be included, go somewhere else for breakfast. You will have the SAME food for breakfast everyday. Dried/semicold eggs, low quality bacon, ham which is sliced as you arrive - not bad, but I wouldn't' choose to eat ham every day. The papaya was the only thing I enjoyed daily - we LOVE papaya. The coffee is TERRIBLE - burnt and week. In fact we went to starbux everyday. We ate lunch at the shore bird once. Had a burger which wasn't bad, but overpriced. We went to the bar at the restaurant one night and had an appetizer with drinks before dinner at another restaurant - sashimi was pretty good. There is entertainment nightly, which gave the bar a nice relaxed feel. Lots of nearby restaurants. I would recommend venturing out of the hotel to eat. Overall, if you are on a budget it's not terrible, but if you're looking for the royal treatment, and exceptional rooms you'll have to buck up and pay Waikiki prices elsewhere, or stay further outside of Waikiki.

<Author>dreducation3
<Content>a good place to stay but be aware... We stayed here with our 3 children, ages 6, 8, and 14, during our vacation. The hotel is nice, but we would not stay here again. Be aware that this review is coming from a family who travels a lot and have stayed in many hotels, so we tend to be a bit more discriminating and require more than a comfortable bed. Okay, the good first: the room was spacious and the staff accomodating. There was plenty of storage space in the room, far more than most hotels. The other side (not necessarily a bad, but instead, these are things to be aware of): there is no Wi-Fi in the room so you have to sit in the lobby to use the internet. The reception was weak at best and at times completely inaccessible no matter where we moved to within the lobby so we ended up surrendering and paying to use the T-mobile hotspot in Starbucks within the hotel. While we were on vacation and not in Hawaii for business, we are a professional couple and needed to check in with work now and then via email, so if you need to be wired to technology or want to surf the net from your room, this is not the hotel for you. Also, this is an older hotel that is undergoing renovations (we heard no noise, a big plus), so maybe their technology will be updated with the cosmetic atmosphere of the hotel. The dining options within the hotel are limited (one where you cook your own food, which takes a while and can be fun or annoying, depending on how hungry you are. We did eat at that restaurant and the food was great. The other choice is an upscale restaurant with a very well-rounded, nice seafood menu. It is much more expensive ($25-40 per meal) but be aware that it's not a quick meal nor well-suited for young children). There are restaurants like Denny's, TGI Friday's and Planet Hollywood within walking distance; however, our family didn't want to eat at a restaurant we could dine in at home -- we were looking for non-chain restaurants unique to Honolulu, so the lack of choices within walking distance was a bit disappointing. There is a lot of construction going on and based on the temporary signs in windows, other dining choices will be opening in the near future. The pool is small and outdated compared to most other hotels, and the rooms are also outdated but very comfortable. The TV is very small, there is no tub, the shower was a bit rusty, and the view in the oceanview rooms provides a partial view of the ocean at best. (The bellman said we should consider ourselves lucky, but for $300+ a night we didn't feel so lucky). The hotel is located very close to the beach, which was very convenient and unlike most others in Honolulu. The activities director on duty at all times was helpful but provided biased advice and direction. It felt like they were serving their own needs instead of providing us with all options we eventually discovered doing our own calling and internet searches. Last, a BIG HINT: if you plan on traveling around the island at all, RENT A CAR!! We did and saved a lot of money. On-site hotel transportation charges $20 per person to take you to Pearl Harbor, the Polynesian Center, etc. Even the Hanaumu Bay, which was a 20 minute drive, cost $15 per person for transportation only if you book through the hotel activities desk. (A cab ride was estimated to be $40-45). Overall, it's a nice hotel and more than acceptable if you're using it for a place to lay your head comfortably. If you're looking for varied amenities or if you need a little more than the basics in a hotel, you'll want to look elsewhere.

<Author>wjb46
<Content>You won't be disappointed! Within this year I have stayed at both the Outrigger on the Beach and the Outrigger on the Reef on Waikiki. I would recommend either of them but recognize differences which people may find necessary to know about before their stay; but they should also be honest about their own needs. At both hotels we stayed in partial ocean view rooms, the Beach was closer to the water but the Reef overlooked the Pool/Hot Tub area which was open to 10PM.  The Outrigger on the Beach is a four star hotel, from the moment you take the escalator to the second floor lobby and sit down to check in, you know you鈥檙e in for a better life鈥檚 experience. The renovations are newer, rooms are larger, and the bathtub was separated into another room in the bathroom, and the breakfast buffet has more choices, Duke鈥檚 is reasonable (for Hawaii) and fine Dinning is available upstairs. We fell asleep to the lapping of the waves (after Dukes closed, it seemed like midnight) but had to close the lanai door when services began delivery at 5:30AM. Everyone loves this hotel, which is part of the criticism. Everything is crowded. You wait for elevators, you wait for restaurant tables, you wait four deep at the bar. Get to the pool early to reserve your lounge chair or to the beach to rent your umbrella and chairs. But its fun! Everyone is so nice and most of the staff makes your feel welcomed. You can always escape the chaos by going to the bar upstairs which is hardly ever crowded; perhaps due to the bartenders who spend most of their time talking to each other.This hotel is on the main street paralleling the beach. Walk out the front door and you have other hotels, restaurants, and every level of shopping. But, walk out the back of the hotel, past Dukes and the pool and the beautiful beach, ocean and view of Diamondhead spread out before you.The Reef is further from the center of Waikiki, but the view may even be better. It is a little more hidden three star hotel under renovation. Two of the three towers were gutted as of 12/06. There were no crowds; it was great! We enjoyed the Hula dancers and music until 10:30 as we sat on our lanai. Sitting on the around the pool or getting and umbrella was never a problem. The water here has more coral in it. The hotel is the second building form Derussey Park and it鈥檚 a great place to take a walk or sight see, a cultural tour even starts in this hotel twice a week. Meals are good but don鈥檛 go to the Shore Bird unless you are going to grill your own meal; we waited half an hour before this news was sprung upon us and the wind was blowing so the smoke filled the restaurant. The Ocean House though is exquisite. We got there when it opened at five, got a fantastic seat, and dined while watching the sun set into the ocean at 5:45. Service was perfect and even the sight error in my custom meal was corrected quickly. All this will change when Trump builds his monstrosity with 2100 condos just behind this hotel, the completion of the two towers and another adjacent hotel to be completed. So get there soon, enjoy it and able to say,鈥滻 remember when鈥︹€?br/>

<Author>M123456
<Content>Old but clean, nice location but noisy We stayed at the this hotel from November 22 - 26, 2006.We booked this hotel through hotwire which meant we did not learn the hotel's name until we paid for it. It is within walking distance of all the Waikiki restaurants and shops. It is right on the beach. There are some rocks in the water so water shoes would be a good idea.The staff was friendly and helpful. We ate at the Reef for Thanksgiving and the food was good. We also ate at the breakfast buffet which was not worth the money.The room was out of date decor wise. The shower and bathroom were extremely small. However the room was clean - it was not as bad as I expected from reading the reviews. I imagine some rooms are in better shape than others.The most important thing for visitors to know is that there are three construction projects going on around the Reef. Directly across the street the Embassy Suites is being built. According to the front desk staff construction on this will be done by the end of the year. The second is also across the street from the Reef. This is the Trump Towers. They just started that project so it has a long way to go. The third is on the Reef itself. They have completely gutted one of their building (the one closest to the ocean) and are in the process of renovating it. Our room was a partial ocean view and faced the construction on the Reef which was the most noisy from our location. Luckily we were there over Thanksgiving so construction was at a minimum. This hotel is old and dated but friendly and clean. It has a great location. If construction noise bothers you I would suggest staying somewhere else.

<Author>nic326
<Content>Always Pleased! I have stayed at The Outrigger Reef the past 4 times I've been to Hawaii and it's always been great. The hotel is a little older but it's in a super location, on the Waikiki Strip but at the very end and up one block so you don't have all the noise and foot traffic. They are in the process of building the Trump Tower which is literally a stone's throw away so if you don't like construction noise, don't stay here.In the event that one does there is quite a bit to do. Hilton Hawaiian Village is a short walk where they have great shopping and restaurants. Most of the designer stores (Gucci, Vuitton, Armani) are up a couple of blocks from the hotel. They have 2 restaurants, The Shore Bird is an open air place for those that want a quick breakfast or lunch and The Ocean Restaurant for a nicer touch - both are right on the beach and have amazing views of the sunset and Diamond Head. The beach is good, nice and clean. Staff are great! They have a little cabana they hang out in all day and come by every now and then to mist you when it gets hot. They also are helpful in answering any questions you have. Chairs and umbrellas are available for $15 per day. You are free to leave, have lunch and still have your chair waiting for you!The hotel has two bars/lounges - one in the lobby near the pool and one in the Shore Bird. Lobby bar is nice if you like a less crowded scene, Shore Bird Bar gets really packed most nights but is really fun. They also feature live music.Make sure you step out to the beach at dusk for the Hilton Hawaiian Village fireworks on Friday nights! It's kind of a fun treat. They also show first run movies on the opposite end of the beach (across the street from the zoo) on Friday nights complete with huge screen and chairs.Rooms are a little dated but CLEAN. Bathrooms can be small but hopefully most of your stay isn't in the room! Service is great and timely. Staff always willing to get extra towels or wait to clean your room if need be. This hotel is also pretty reasonably priced, especially for the location. So I reccomend waiting for Trump to finish then take a trip to Outrigger Reef!

I think it's obvious that I do not recommend this hotel if your expecting a 4 star rating. They rate this higher on some sites then the Hyatt Waikiki, how ? The price for this hotel is really cheap so it makes it appealing. On my first trip with four girlfriends we were only there for 3 days so I did'nt get a chance to take in the hotel. The second trip I definitely took it in and decided after a chain of events that it was'nt worth the discount. The third trip, not by choice, was the last. I hope this helps.

<Content>Decent Hotel, but be wary of construction This was my 3rd time staying at a hotel in Waikiki. Sailboats  catermerans stop just outfront on the hotel beach and you can book rides on them daily. The hotel pool was large and decent, but often crowded and there are 3 hot tubs that were so hot I rarely saw anyone sitting in them for more than a few minutes. We ate at the Chief's Hut once and the Shoreline twice. Both very casual - we saved our big nights out for other places like Hoku's (at the Kahala) and the Hanohano Room (at the Sheraton). Our room in the Pacific Tower was definitely in need of some renovation but it was very clean. I requested two beds and was given that plus a couch that pulled out into another. Perfect as we were 3 female friends sharing the room. The bathroom was very small and only had a shower. Our room had a nice balcony but it was impossible to sit out on it during the weekday because of the loud construction. On the weekends  at night it was fine if one can get over the eyesore of a giant empty lot in front of you. The entire staff at the hotel was extremely friendly and accomodating. I liked the shops in the lobby and I very much enjoyed the calendar of free activities the hotel offers. We tried the Friday morning hula class and had a fun time. We found out that the lobby will begin major renovation/construction on 10/1/06. So be warned about this. Outside of the construction it was fine. We hardly spent any time at the hotel anyway as we were driving all over the island.

<Content>Disappointed in the room quality We just returned from a stay at Outrigger Reef, which was an add on to our week in Kauai. What a letdown. I chose this hotel because we had stayed next door at the Waikiki Shores a few years back and liked the lobby and pool area, which we were allowed to use. Since we were unable to get a room at the Shores, I thought I'd try Outrigger Reef. I felt the quality of the lobby/pool area was a good indication of what I could expect from the rooms. Boy, was I mistaken! Granted, I chose one of the cheaper rooms. It was in the the tower overlooking the pool on the 10th floor. I knew it would be small and without a great view, but expected it to be in good condition and clean. The first room we were in (non-smoking) smelled of stale smoke. It was not all that clean and the bathroom was in poor condition. The tile in the very small shower had been painted white and was chipped and peeling. The vanity was also chipped and peeling from water damage. The bathroom floor and the carpet in the room was not very clean. We complained and were moved to a different room on the 11th floor. It was slightly better (no smoke smell) and a little cleaner, but the bathroom was still in the same poor shape. At night, we were treated to bad hawaiian music from the band that played all evening until midnight or later. The construction across the street was noisy and made getting in and out of the hotel driveway a challenge. The valet parking was pricy ($18/day). And it would have been nice to have a microwave in the room to save on eating out.On a positive note, I requested extra towels and pillows and they were promptly provided and replenished in the room by the maid daily. The staff was courteous, helpful and responsive. We enjoyed breakfast daily at the Chief's Hut. The daily specials were a fantastic deal (4.99). We enjoyed a great lunch at the Shore Bird (we did not order the buffet, it didn't look too good). The hotel was conveniently located on the beach and within walking distance of many restaurants, shopping and of course your choice of several ABC stores! The pool was nice and not over crowded the time we spent there.Although I've had very good experience with Outrigger overall on many occasions, I would not recommend the Outrigger Reef. Instead, try the Waikiki Shores next door and book through Outrigger (not Castle). Be sure you get the deal that allows you use of the Outrigger Reef facilities. That way, you have the best of both worlds. A great room with full kitchen facilities and the amenities afforded by the hotel next door!

The Shore Bird restaurant is beachside and was great fun as we grilled our own steaks with the help of our waiter and which were excellent. We also had dinner in the Ocean View restaurant with excelllent dining. I ordered a macadamia nut crusted mahi mahi with a garlic cream sauce over pasta surrounded with shrimp and scallops - delicious!! As none of us had ever been to Hawaii, we wanted to do tourist things and also have time to relax on the beach. The activities desk was very helpful helping us plan our tours. We snorkled at Hanauma Bay, took a bus tour around the island including the North Shore, went to a luau at Paradise Cove, went horseback riding and visited the Polynesian Culture Center and saw the show. I definately recommend the Outrigger Reef.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good value for money and a great position Our party (2 couples and 1 teenager) stayed at the hotel for six nights after spending 10 days skiing and sightseeing on the West Coast.We were all a bit apprehensive after reading some of the reviews but were pleasantly surprised.Yes there is building work going on at the back of the hotel but as far as we were concerned this was not an issue when the balcony windows were closed and was more than compensated for by the position of the hotel, which was great. Honolulu was a lot bigger and busier than we had expected so there are many hotels now which do not have either a beach position or even an ocean view. The Outrigger not only has both but being where it is, gets the fantastic sunsets, which the hotels further round towards the Duke's statue on Waikiki Beach do not.Initially my sister and her husband were given a city view room next to the lift. Do not accept one of these, as you will spend far more time awake than asleep. When they complained, they were moved without any problem, so the reception staff are obviously used to this complaint! The room they were moved to did not have a view, but that was the only problem. The family room that my family were in had a partial ocean view room overlooking the pool - the view on the balcony one way was towards the building site but the other looked directly towards the ocean and was great. The rooms were a reasonable size and were kept very clean. The bathrooms were a bit dated but again were clean and the showers great. There was tea and coffee making facilities in the room which was much appreciated.We ate in the Ocean House 4 times and twice in the Shore Bird - 2 very different types of meal. The Ocean House was very, very good but not cheap. The food was excellent - none of us had a bad meal/course. It is worth asking about the specials as they were particularly good. The staff were very obliging and on the occasions we asked for an ocean-front table, we were given one. The Shore Bird (DIY) had a very good menu and was markedly cheaper but would not suit if you don't like barbeques! It is worth eating in the hotel at least once, just to see the sunset. People gather on the beach in front of the Ocean House just to watch them. Just check the sunset time as it happens rather fast! Please note, however, that it is worth booking well in advance (up to a day!) - particularly for the Ocean House.The lifts were a bit unpredictable - as with all hotels on the beach, you need a room key to operate them, so it was a bit of a challenge to get the key in before the lift had gone too far! Overall, we were more than happy. All the staff were very polite and willing to help when asked. The hotel was very clean and had a good variety of shops on the ground floor, including a Starbucks and Jamba Juice.

<Content>Great Stay at the Outrigger Reef Just returned tonight from the Outrigger Reef and had a great stay. Our first two nights were spent at the other end of the beach where even without construction it is MUCH noisier. The Outrigger Reef is away from Kalakua so you don't get the constant hum of traffic, sirens etc. And the beach to the Hilton side of the hotel is huge and sandy if you want to get out of the rocks. One must do is to walk to the Hilton Hawaiian Village (short walk) on Friday night and check out the free show and fireworks. One maybe/maybe not is the Outrigger Catamaran - make sure you get a coupon, barely worth the $20 never mind the $30 they ask without coupon. They will try and talk you into the $5 shaker (+$2 for the drink) instead of the $2 cocktails - big ripoff. Pretty sure it was straight juice - enjoy the ride, forget the drinks. Or have a pop for $1. Still a decent ride on the ocean but only go on a HOT day when the splash of the ocean would be refreshing and fun rather than just cold. Also, wasn't a big fan of the Shorebird, though many are. Very smokey where you cook your meat, and the person at the grill wasn't all that helpful about how to cook the MahiMahi. Maybe just a bad night. We enjoyed the Chief's Hut much better - reasonably priced, music in the evening, by the waterfalls/lagoon. All in all, we really enjoyed our stay - quiet end of the beach, great staff, would love to go back when the beachwalk is done construction. Wouldn't hesitate to stay again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Teeny, clean room (also mention some Oahu tips) My husband and I stayed in a partial ocean-view room for one night. The hotel is in an area with a great deal of construction, and the beach access is convenient, but not the best of beaches. Take a walk just a bit further down, and find a cleaner (and quieter) beach. Or, better yet, go to Hanauma Bay (more on that later). The staff was *very* friendly, except those that work at the travel desk. When we arrived, we were told that they had little information about our needs (we had booked on Priceline, and had been quoted for a room with one king or two double-beds). They upgraded us to a non-smoking, king room with a partial-ocean view. There is free wireless at this hotel, in the lobby only. Just ask the front desk for a 'code.'  The hotel was busy with the tourist crowd, but the room was quiet, albeit small. The bed took up about 2/3 of the room! :) A few highlights for your trip:- Sam Choy's restaurant is AMAZING for a fine dining experience (Pacific Rim cuisine)- Visit 'Leonard's Bakery' for fresh, hot malasadas (Portugese pastries)- Seabird Tours - coupon in 'Best of Oahu' (pick up at concierge desk or in lobby) for $12 round trip transport and gear to snorkel at Hanauma Bay- Polynesian Cultural Center - don't spend extra for the 'Ambassador' package unless you can't navigate yourself around a theme park; don't take a tour with Rob (Samoa)- Paradise Cove luau is MUCH better than the one at the Polynesian Cultural Center, or anywhere else!- Chinatown is a lot of fun for an afternoon walk or for a photo-shoot- Go to Hanauma Bay early, early in the morning (otherwise the water becomes cloudy from swimmers)- Take a hike with 'Oahu Nature Tours' - Mike, the owner, is extremely knowledgeable and helpfulHave a wonderful time! Aloha!

After reading all these reviews I wasn't sure what to expect, but it turned out not too bad after all. The employees are more then friendly, we were honeymooning and they sent us a bottle of champange and macadamia nuts complientary which was sweet. When we got to our room though, I wasn't too pleased. It was a standard room, not even a balcony. I didn't really feel like I was in Hawaii it just seemed like a standard Holiday Inn, except the difference is Holiday Inn's are $60 a night, unlike this $255 a room. So after a few complaints to my husband, he went to the front desk and upgraded our room for an extra $40 a night. It was well worth it we were on the 4th floor overlooking the pool, the room was twice the size of the first room. Overall after that I was pleased. The only negative side of the hotel was the bathrooms, they were small and looked pretty old and could use some remodeling.Other then that, I was really pleased with the hotel room. I mean we couldn't beat the location it was right on Waikiki beach. The restaurants are good, we would eat at Chiefs Hut every morning for the breakfast special since it was only $4.99 everyday and different varieties. The Shorebird was nice, except be prepared to cook your own meat. I think it's fun but others might not agree. They have great lava flows for drinks and entertainment at nighttime.The hotel also has other needs like gift shops and a pantry right on the ground level. This hotel isn't a five star by any means, but if your not to picky and want a hotel close to the beach I recommend this hotel. Would i stay here again? Probably not only because my husband is in the military and we can get fantastic rates at the Hale Koa next door to the Reef. If were weren't though I would consider it again. I've stayed at the Hiliton Hawaiian Village and as standard as the Ohana Islander Hotel so all in all it was a great trip and were already planning a return to the island next year. Were 22 and 23 years old but this is one thing that we like to do is travel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Wonderful holiday We stayed at Outrigger Reef on the Beach in Honolulu and absolutely loved it. We don't usually stay in the better hotels but because I have some problems with walking as the day progresses we decided that we needed to pick a hotel on the beach. We read a lot of reviews indicating that the rooms were small etc. so we were somewhat worried. We asked for a non-smoking, kingsize bed in a lower cost standard room. When we arrived the room was a smoking room with a queen-size bed and they explained that the requested room is never guaranteed. I was a bit disappointed but we had a balcony and if you looked to the left, you could see the ocean and beach. It wasn't a big stretch of ocean but we didn't pay for an ocean-view room so we were pleasantly surprised. We could hear the ocean and that was a real plus.We'd heard about the construction and how noisy it was but though it is true that there is a lot of construction in the Waikiki area, we didn't choose to let it bother us. We heard the ocean and not the construction. It was wonderful to be able to step out of the hotel and step onto the beach. I would recommend that you take along some beach shoes because the rocks in the water are bad on your feet.It is true that you pay $30.00 a day to rent two chairs and an umbrella for the day but that is a choice that you make. The pool and pool area are wonderful and there were always chairs available.My husband took a free pool scuba-diving lesson. Get a letter from your doctor if you have high blood pressure and want to take the lesson.Our cleaning lady was wonderful and we left her $3.00 on our pillow daily.The hotel gave us free champagne because it was our 35th anniversary. Because we decided to extend our visit another 5 days,they also gave us one free land lesson for surfing and a free two hour rental of a surf board that my husband really appreciated. We were close to a Denny's and were able to walk to many other eating locations that were not too highly priced. It is true that Hawaii is expensive but we knew that before we went. I would definitely stay in this hotel again if the price doesn't go up for the cheaper rooms. We can't afford the more expensive rooms.

<Author>Jdublyou
<Content>More thn pleasantly surprised After reading hundreds of reviews for this hotel, we were cautiously optimistic and now, pleasantly surprised. My wife, 5 year old daughter and I expected a spartan room but great beach access. The Reef was sold out due to the golf tournament, but we were delighted to get a complimentary upgrade to a City View (junior) suite, that overlooked the pool area and had a nice sidelong view of the beach. Very cool little lanai to sit in the evenings and settle in after the day and before dinner.Many of the reviews we read spoke to a certain deterioration of the property; particularly the rooms and bathrooms. Yep. They're small and they were small when they were built. But we found that the 'lived in' quality of the overall facility lent itself to a certain character that we enjoyed. We've stayed in budget hotels in Acapulco and 5 stars on the Mayan Riviera. I don't know, but the high end resorts tend to have a sterile quality and the dives are an exercise in 'getting what you pay for. I thought the O Reef was a nice compromise.The absolute defining factor was the staff. These people work hard and genuinely make you feel welcome. Example: Our maid, Lori became a friend, always asking our daughter about her day. I felt badly about getting sand on the carpet from a beach bag. I didn't notice it til I picked up the bag to go back to the beach the next day. On the way out I mentioned it to Lori and she said...You have a great vacation....I'll worry about the sand!One anomaly for us was the Shorebird. It looked like a cool restaurant but always a tedious wait for a good reservation. I am willing to acknowledge that we may have just gotten there on a bad night. But my thoughts upon leaving the one night we did eat there was that Customer service stops at their front door. It might have been that we were spoiled by the rest of the hotel staff, but we found the shorebird employees were officious, curt and generally not helpful. From the hostess to the server we felt that we were just bodies moving through and they were more interested in just getting us fed and out the door and on to their next tip. It is hugely over priced and there are many very good restaurants within walking distance. But, you don't get the spectacular view of the beach at sunset. My suggestion if you want to go there, make an early reservation and bring a huge appetite, resist the pressure to order and eat quickly and make the most of a very pricey meal with indifferent staff. Of note: our server volunteered that the Shorebird was a separate entity from the hotel itself and I guess that was to explain why the service was less than acceptable.Conversely, the Chief's Hut is a hoot. Prices are reasonable, the staff is great and if you go there for breakfast, please say 'aloha' to the hostess Gail for us. She is wonderful. So is the Mahi Mahi.We tried a few of the excursions. I won't do that again. For the most part, our best moments were on the beach or the pool at the hotel and just walking around to see the sights. The tours we took were so structured and confined that we felt like calves in a cattle drive. Suggestion: If you want to take a tour or see the sights, such as Hanauma Bay (highly recommended for snorkeling) or Pearl Harbor, rent a car for the day and avoid the necessary control issues, the high prices and the extra time that an organized tour requires.Overall we had a great time. As is the sign of any good vacation, it was just too short.It is a comfortable, quality place to retreat from a cold winter. The people there are a treat. We'll go back and stay longer.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>I never wanted to leave I just returned from a wonderful week in Waikiki Beach. The Outrigger Reef Hotel was perfect for my traveling group. The hotel is located on the beach,right in the middle of lots of activities ie;sailboat rides,surfing lessons,kayak rentals,etc.The staff was incredibly nice and helpful.There are 3 activity booths on site to make tour/day trip plans with,and all were very helpful.The hotel has a casual, friendly atmosphere, 3 resturants,2 bars and several shops all located around the open air lobby. I booked thru a conference and the rates were very reasonable $168 per night for a 2nd floor room with a private patio that opened up to a larger terrace w/lounge chairs that over looked the pool...the regular rate for that room was only $195 per night (week of 11/12-11/19). Our room was large w/2 dble beds,pull out sofa,table and 2 chairs.and a decent sized bathroom. We were flying out late night so for $100 we got a late check-out room until 6:00pm.That was on the 11th floor...next to elevator..much smaller room,but ok for a couple on a budget. There is still construction going on across the street,but our rooms were right across the street and we couldn't hear it at all when our patio door was closed (sleeping in the a.m.)The hotel is within walking distance to all the best shopping in Waikiki,from Chanel to the International Market and 100's of places to eat (Denny's or McDonalds are across the street for fast,cheap food)...I had a great time not only exploring all that Oahu has to offer..but the staff and the visitors at the hotel and everywhere we went on the island made us feel like these are our friends and this is our home even though we only spent 1 week in Oahu. The genorosity and spirit of the people of Hawaii was just as unforgettable as the breathtaking landscape of the island.

<Author>AlaninOz
<Content>Go there - its great! I was in Hawaii for three weeks - stayed the first 10 days at the Outrigger Reef. You could not find a better Hotel.My room was rather small but you get what you pay for but I did have Ocean/beach views. The room was clean and the maid very friendly. The pool area is small for the hotel but you get that and there is always the beach, however they do charge $30 for a beach bed. The Shorebird bar and Restaurant must not be missed. The greatest of views ever. All you can eat Breakfast is $11-40 but there are various vouchers around with $1 off. The place was very full and very busy.As for the construction work - yes it is all happenning but the work/noise is not intrusive. There is more noise eminating from Tour Buses and Hotel delivery trucks than construction site vehicles - don't let it bother you.Here are some Oahu tips:Best Seafood - either Pacific Beach Hotel (all you can eat buffet for $25) or Bubba Gumps on the 4th floor at the Aloa Moana Shopping Centre.Best Pub - Moose Mcgillycuddys in Lewers Street - Good food too!Sea Life Park - Thought a bit Amateurish but good for the kids - use the trolly blue line ($25) for a 3 hour round trip there with plenty of stop offs (Diamond Head Crater and beaches etc)For Pearl Harbor use the shuttle its only $11 and if you go on Wednesday/Saturday or Sunday the ladies can also go to the Aloha Markets where you can get the cheapest of things.Chinese food - J.R.'s smogasbord in the Hawaii International Market Place only $12-50 for dinner, around 30 dishes plus soft drinks and fresh fruit.Do a bus tour around the Island (around $50) the only problem is that they do not stop at a lot of places because buses are not allowed to stop there. Find out the history, then hire a car and go back there for your picture shoot etc.Polynesian Cultural Center - Two days required for this (your pass will allow you to go back again) a long day but worth it - make sure you go to the Samoan Village, the guy is a real crack up! the evening show is brilliant.I could go on but feel I have said enough, enjoy your trip, enjoy your stay at the Reef and I guarantee you will return.

<Author>ajaj
<Content>Outrigger Reef much more than expected Just returned from our stay at the Outrigger on the Reef from Sept 17 through Sept 25, actually suppose to have left on Sept 24 but we were stranded in Paradise due to Hurricane Rita. Eleven of us went for the wedding of our daughter on Sept 20. I had been concerned very much from the reviews about construction and small dirty rooms. I had read about upgrades but prior to leaving many of the hotels in the area, including the Reef, had no availablilty.Upon our arrival, the lobby was huge and wide open. We had reserved 5 rooms, standard rooms, and all were ready except one. When I requested an upgrade for the bride and groom, there were not rooms available. I was still nervous until we got to our rooms. The bride was given a mini-suite and the rest of our rooms were clean and beautiful. We were in the Ocean Tower Rooms 901, 902, 903, 905 and 927. Room 905 was the mini suite with a city view. Room 927 was our room and it had a partial ocean view, which was also beautiful. The surf was really loud at times which was so relaxing. The bathroom was small, only a shower but it was very clean. I had read review about black mold and mildew in the showers. There was none in ours. The other rooms were further back from the ocean but you could still see the ocean from the balony. Also the 9th and 10th floors have an express elevator to the ninth floor. People on the tenth floor then walked up about 7 steps and were in the 10th floor.We could get off our elevator and nealy on the beach. The beach does have rocks, reef-like rocks--not smooth rocks, so bring your swim shoes or get some at the ABC store. I bought mine at the ABC store for $14 and they were worth it. I also used them when we went snorkeling at Hanuuama Bay.The pool is not really big but plenty of chairs when we were there. The pool is a salt water pool, not like back home in Louisiana.Bring your walking shoes. You will walk alot.The Shorebird: we had breakfast buffett for $9 and it was good but we only did this for one morning. Had lunch there one day hamburger $8.99, fries (enough for 2 people)$3 and coke $3. The view was great! It is directly on the beach. It is open to air and was not hot due to the breeze. The Cheifs Hut breakfast for about $5 per person and it was filling. We liked Starbucks most morings because it was fairly quick to get and cimamion roll and drink to go. McDonald directly across the road and Dennys to the right.Other restraunts: Toaido's buffett with snow crab legs and fried shrimp, desserts and 40 kinds of sushi. Even if you don't like sushi, which we did not, their was plenty of items for $26 per person. Also Bubba Gumps in the Ala Monia Mall was great, both food and service. Price range $15-20 per person and way more than you can eat. Two couples went to the Cheesecake Factory and said it was great. We went to plantet hollywood, prices like the Shorebird for lunch.We saw: Germaine's LuauPearl Harbor full tourSociety of SevenPolyneasin Magic ShowThe most beautiful wedding on Diamond Head Beach at sunset.The Outrigger Reef was more that I expected for the the price $148 per night. The maid was very nice and did a good job. The concergie was very helpful with directions and information. We were also delayed b one day due to the Houston airport being shut down due to Hurricane Rita. I beleive her name was Jennifer and she spoke with the hotel desk and arranged for us to stay in our same rooms for an extra night. We payed the same rate of $148. The Activity Desk is a good place to arrange trips. Pearl Harbor trip $38 I think, we took left at 6am and returned at 2 pm or so. The Polynesian Culture Center, $95 per person for the full trip, there are different prices,leaves at 10 am and returns at 10:30 pm. We did not get to do this one due to running out of time. Snorkel at Hanamuna Bay was good, we did not get in the smooth part but did see several different kinds of fish. My 7-year old grandson learned to snorkel in about 10 minutes and loved it.We would stay at the Reef again, the price was very good for beachfront and our rooms where great in the Ocean Tower.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Information you should know before you book We had booked this hotel as part of a three centre trip - Las Vegas, Hawaii and San Francisco. We were to spend seven nights at this hotel and were really looking forward to spending a relaxing time there. However, on arrival we were given the standard room booked by our travel company as part of the package. The balcony of this small dark room looked straight onto the balcony of the next hotel, just 10 ft. separated us. Also, it was next to the noisy lift so we decided not to unpack and to change it. We were shown to a partial ocean view room - the other partial view was of the road they are building behind the beach area, with all the accompanying noise, especially in the early morning!! Finally, we decided to bite on the bullet and upgrade to a superior room - the hotel kindly decided to charge us only 50% of the upgrade price, which was appreciated. The room was light and airy and had a beautiful view of the spectacular beach where this hotel is situated.You should be aware that across the road from the front of the hotel, they are knocking down another hotel. You can hear the noise from the swimming pool area, so its not an area for peace and quiet - also the restaurant by the pool suffers from the noise and disruption. This was not pointed out by our travel company and if we had known about this, we would have booked an alternative hotel.That said, the beach at the back of the hotel is spectacular and the fine dining restaurant which overlooks the beach is equal to any five star restaurant - try to get a beachside table when you reserve, you can't get a table without reserving at least one day in advance especially on weekends.Try to get out of Honolulu for a trip around the island, there are some awesome sights and beautiful beaches - Honolulu is very high-rise and not what we expected but outside the city is worth seeing.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Fantastic location, average hotel We visited the outrigger reef 7th - 17th July 05 as part of our honeymoon. On arriving at the hotel we were told that there were no upgrades available so we made our way to the standard room that we had booked. We were less than happy with the room we had been given as the balcony looked straight out onto the hotel opposite, which was approximately 10 feet away! This made the small room very dark and the bathroom was a joke. You could hardly even turn around in it! On top of this we were right next to the elevator and after being in the room 5 minutes we were already irritated by the noise!However, it does get better! We returned to the desk to ask to be changed to a different room and without even asking we were upgraded to a garden terrace room. The room itself was much bigger than the first one, and the bathroom and bed were also bigger. Unfortunately the room looked out onto the Mcdonald's and building site opposite the hotel, so during the day it did get quite noisy but we were able to put up with this as we weren't in the room much, and we were grateful for being upgraded anyway after seeing the standard rooms! I think if we had been on another side of the hotel the noise from the building works would not have been an issue.The lobby is very nice and spacious but the rest of the hotel desperately needs an upgrade. Walking through the corridors to the room was like walking back to the 1970's! The rooms were slightly better but could have also done with decorating. However overall the room was clean and the maid service was very good. All staff at the hotel were very friendly. The location of the hotel is excellent. Being right on the beach was fantastic and to get to the main shopping part of Waikiki is only a few minutes walk away. There are plenty of shops and restaurants nearby. Overall we had a great time at the outrigger reef but we thought the hotel was average. I'm sure if you're willing to pay the top prices for the ocean view rooms then this hotel would be a great place to stay. In the end we got a fairly nice room and very much enjoyed our holiday!

<Author>Angry Clive Man
<Content>Just another day in paradise Reading many of these reviews, it seems like the experience people have is very much hit or miss. You love this place or you hate it.We got lucky. We just spent seven nights in the Diamond Head tower. Our room was in the city view category, which is only one notch up from the lowest category. So we were very surprised that our deck had gorgeous views of both the ocean and the pool.The room was immaculate and although it was not large, it was comfortable. The bathroom is quite small, but if you only have one person in there at a time, it is not an issue. Trying to fit two people in that bathroom at a time would have been impossible.The hotel is located right on the beach, with plenty of activities offered everyday. For instance, there is a catamaran ride offered on the beach just outside the hotel for only $15 for a one-hour trip. It was a blast.The biggest issue at the hotel is the surrounding construction. They are tearing down several nearby hotels, and it creates quite a traffic bottleneck in front of the hotel. But I'd disagree with previous comments that the construction noise is so loud that it disrupts life at the hotel. Sitting around the pool you can hardly hear it. And at the beach it is far enough away that it is a non-issue. The bigger issue is when you leave the hotel to go shopping and have to walk through the construction zone. There was one day that the noise was so loud that people were covering their ears. But in the grand scheme of things this is a minor distraction.The hotel pool was great, and the pool staff very friendly. The hotel offers a wonderful breakfast buffet, in a great location overlooking the ocean.Another comment that I had read was that the timeshare salespeople in the hotel lobby are annoying. All they do is try to engage you in a conversation. If you ignore them, it is not an issue. In a week's stay, I probably had four such encounters. It is no big deal.There is a constant parade of free Hawaiian entertainment in the hotel lobby, the rooms are clean and safe and quiet, the staff is helpful, and the location is outstanding.This place was terrific.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>The Only Place to Stay in Waikiki! This is the only hotel my family and I will stay at in Honolulu. Over the past fifteen years, we have tried other resorts but none compare to Outrigger Reef on the Beach. From the moment you step on the property, you feel relaxed--from the friendly staff (much nicer than the staff at *luxury* hotels at which I've stayed) to the baskets of free flowers (plumeria, orchids, tuberose) in the lobby--you know you're in paradise! I've always stayed in Partial Ocean View rooms without complaint--gorgeous views and clean, comfortable surroundings. Be sure to check out the turtle/koi fish pond next to the pool--kids love it!Chief's Hut Restaurant provides great, affordable meals under the Waikiki moon and dinner at the Shorebird is a nice splurge for your wallet and your waistline. However you absolutely must try Shorebird's breakfast buffet. It is the most economical and delicious breakfast I have ever had--and you can't beat the view of Diamond Head in the morning sunshine. Very memorable!The hotel is within blocks of all the to do sites in Waikiki and there is even a new Starbucks on the property to keep you energized for sightseeing. I guarantee that Outrigger Reef will enhance your next Honolulu vacation--and you will treasure your Hawaiian memories.

The shorebird has excellent food and you can grill your own steaks while looking out at the ocean since it sits on the beach. And the price is pretty average with other steak houses in waikiki. While on Oahu try to get to the flea market at the aloha stadium. If you have no car, take the bus or shuttle. The hotel activities desk can tell you how. This is the best place to save money on souveniers( 8 tshirts for 20., 7puka shell necklaces for 5.) Believe me, there is no place better and I have lived on Oahu for 17 years. Even the locals go here to shop. The Outrigger is a great place and we would reccommend it to anyone. Please fell free to e-mail with any questions.

<Author>Marti
<Content>Nice place! Hope to stay there again! We just got back from a 10-day vacation to Oahu; 5 of which we spent at the Outrigger Reef.Pros: a beautiful hotel; nice pool; great beach location; great location, period; nice rooms; great deal (internet site averaged $107/nt for their smallest room, which was quite adequate and had nice park views); Starbucks in lobby opens early; restaurants on site are nice and a decent value; shops in lobby are nice; quiet room (despite the fact we were adjacent to the elevator, we heard no elevator noise!); the beach/surf was very nice and calm and I saw a surprising amount of reef fish while snorkeling; there were 3 hot tubs (2 that are separate, elevated from the pool level and one attached to the pool); there is an adequate amount of pool lounge chairs.Cons: it is true that there is demolition going on in the area. The beach has lots of rocks/coral and I would recommend wearing footwear if you're going to swim. The beach itself is very short and there is an additional charge for lounge chairs and umbrellas.Overall, we had a great experience and would go back to this hotel.

We called the Hotel Manager and were politely advised that the hotel was now fully booked but to call back in 2 days time to see if we could move to another room, ok we thought - let's just get on with it, however 1 hour later we strolled through the reception area to see a family of none Europeans asking if they had any vacancies for 3 nights. The answer was Yes Sir, would you like an Ocean view? We then immediately asked for a transfer of room which was granted, the room still didn't come anywhere near the rooms we had seen the week before in San Francisco - Alcatraz comes to mind! We tried to enjoy our weeks stay in Hawaii spending our days on the beach and evenings in the Shorebird Bar which did have some very talented bands and vocalists to be fair. I have to say that the American customers are more highly thought of than Europeans and this is evidenced in the superior rooms and by far better service they receive. We have both travelled the world extensively and can safely say that this is probably the worst Hotel we have stayed in yet, on our travels around he US we have visited 14 States which all bar one we have rated very highly. Very Disappointed - we didn't even see Magnum but think we saw TC and Higgins in an Italian restaurant one night! <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>What a difference a room makes! My daughter and I have now had the opportunity to stay in four different rooms at this hotel between October 2003 and April 2005. We have stayed in a high-level partial-ocean view room which had a nice view, two beds, fridge, lanai, but no tub; a 5th floor Pacific Tower corner (Rm 547) non-smoking, which had the other ammenities listed as well as a microwave, some plateware, a small table for four, and a fold-out couch, plus a lanai with no view; a Pacific Tower non-smoking room with no lanai, no tub, no microwave, paper-thin walls, and noisey appliances (RM 1167); and finally a room in the Diamond Head Tower building (Rm 477) on the smoking floor, but with more space, two beds, a shower, lanai, fridge, small table with two chairs, all of which suited a longer stay and if we leaned we could see the ocean from the lanai. We got the Diamond Head Tower room by complaining about #1167 the morning after our first night's stay there. We had five nights to go on our vacation so it was worth it to speak up, and we didn't have to pay for an upgrade. Thank you Matt at the front desk!I recommend the Diamond Head building, which is only four floors and the farthest from the front desk, because it is quieter and close to the pool -- really great if you have a child. We used the starcase in lieu of the elevator all the time. The Third floor is non-smoking, and the fourth floor is smoking, but we were not bothered by the fumes for the most part. If you keep the lanai doors open, you will smell bacon frying in the morning and hear and smell the evening activities at The Shorebird Restaurant, but I swear it all shuts down promptly at 10:30 p.m., even on the weekends.Four rooms later I can say that all the bathrooms at the Outrigger Reef on the Beach are consistently too small and in poor repair. Bed quality was consistently fine, and pillow quality varied from room to room. The location is great for families with kids if you plan to stay in Waikiki. My daughter made several good friends at the pool, and the daily activities, such as lei-making and hula demonstrations, are all ages. For other activities it was easy walking to shopping, other hotel restaurants, and to the bus for outlying excursions. The onsite restaurants are reasonable. Spa prices are competitive for all treatments. Take the Outrigger Catamaran for a great two-hour thrill ride -- we've done the more civilized susnset cruise and the afternoon sail where we got soaked and really got to sail the ocean and interact with the crew.

<Content>Fantastic Our family (2 adults, 1 teen and 1 fourth grader) stayed for 7 nights April, 2004. We were amazed at the attentiveness of the staff and the personality of the hotel. The hotel itself is on the beach far enought away from the hotel lounge scene to have a sense of tropical relaxation but close enough that everything is but a 5 minute walk away. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Room! Stayed at Outrigger Reef on the Beach two nights from 2/24-2/26/05. You're greeted with valet service ($15 a day) that is pretty much manditory considering finding a place to park on the streets of Honolulu is almost impossible. The reception area is very clean and it's openess (no doors) was a great welcoming sight. Upon checking-in we were upgraded from a partial ocean view in the Waikiki tower to a beach front room in the Diamond Head Tower (much larger). You also receive a welcome package with coupons of local merchants and several free postcards of Waikiki. Also included with our room was four free breakfast coupons for ShoreBird restuarant which is located on the main floor of the hotel. The restaurant is a great place to eat! At night you cook your own meat on an open bar overlooking the ocean! What a grillers delight! : ) Our room number was 386. If you want have THE PERFECT ROOM I suggest calling the hotel directly and requesting this room. Since I paid for the partial view room which was $203 a night I'm not sure exactly how much they charge for this room but I guarantee that it would be worth it. Your balcony overlooks the beach and has a perfect view of Diamond Head. Since all my other trips to Hawaii I have stayed with family members that live on the island, I can tell you that staying in Waikiki was quite a change of pace. Staying in Haleiwa before I experienced the more secluded side of Oahu. Waikiki has a Vegas type theme on the main street (which all the major shopping is located...i.e. LV, Prada, Coach etc). Located on the beach are umbrellas and sun chairs with pads are for rent for $10 (set of two chairs and one umbrella with drink holders). Other activities to do on the property are rides on Outrigger Catamarans- one hour for $15 a person...a bargain in Honolulu! This hotel was impressive and I will definitely stay there on future trips to Oahu. I suggest room 386 for anyone looking to have only the best!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Would have liked more sun! We were at the Outrigger Reef on the Beach for eight nights, starting January 28th, 2005.The Outrigger Reef on the Beach is a fine hotel, with friendly, helpful and sincere staff. The rooms were very clean, and well maintained. We read the reviews that said to upgrade your room when you got there. We were originally booked in a Standard Room, and asked to be upgraded. The upgrade costs ranged from $25 per night for the City View Room to $110 per night for an Ocean View Junior Suite. (this was 50% of the original upgrade cost) At eight nights, it made it cost prohibitive, so we decided to upgrade to the City View Room. I'm not sure if that was a great idea. The room overlooked the MacDonald's and you had to put up with fairly loud street noise from trucks, busses, and service vehicles. Sometimes it doesn't pay.The room itself was very clean and we slept well during the entire week. It is close to the bus routes and shopping, but if we ever go back, we will probably stay at the other end of the beach because the beach is better (no rocks) and it doesn't really matter if you stay at a hotel on the beach, since many lower star hotels have better beach views and cost less. The other benefit of staying at the other end of the beach is that most of the trendy bars and entertainment are at that end as well. The Outrigger Reef on the Beach is closer to the shopping areas, so if that's what you like to do, then it is ideal.Speaking of shopping, most of the high-end stores are too expensive for souvenirs, and we fould the best place to buy budegt souvenirs was right in the hotel or at the ABC stores, which are all over.We probably won't go back to Wakiki, because it is very commercial and busy. If you're looking to find Hawaii like it is in the movies, it doesn't exist in Wakiki. That said, we had a fabulous tim, but we would have liked a little more sun.

<Content>Include this Hotel in your short list AlohaWe stayed for 10 nights at the Outrigger Reef Nov14-24 2004 and would go back in a second. Had to wait 3 hours to check- in due to a very busy checkout day ( Sunday ) as guaranteed checkin 3pm and we arrived at 10:30 am in HNL Airport. This was probably the only low-light of our stay and obviously to most waiting in the bar 3 hours by the beach is no hardship - it was only my husband was slightly unwell. This hotel has everything you could need and while some of the 5 star hotels are definitely more polished this hotel is very easy to feel at ease in. The location is also good as it is at the beginning of the strip away from the heart of things and is a great walk down the beach or down Kalakaua Ave. The 'BUS' stop is just across the road. Yes the ocean floor out front is very rocky but for a 50 metre walk down the beach you can feel the white sands of Waikiki ( imported from Australia ) beneath your toes. The pool is one of the biggest in Waikiki, stacks of lounges and very clean.The restaurants are very busy ( that says something) and reservations strongly recommended.The Housekeeping staff ( Level 5 Ocean Tower ) are the epitome of Aloha and our room was always cleaned beautifully. For a slightly above average priced holiday unless you are incredibly fussy and need to be mollycoddled you will love it here! Mahalo

<Author>kymiss
<Content>Can't wait to stay at outrigger again We just returned from our 5 night stay at Outrigger Reef, and it was awesome. We booked an ocean view room and did not regret it, the view of the ocean and Diamond Head was spectacular! We left the wide sliding doors open all night and enjoyed the breeze and sounds of the ocean. Our room was in the Ocean tower (I think that was the name) closest to the beach, because we were on the 9th floor there was an express elevator that did not stop between the lobby floor and floor 9. This made coming and going quick and easy. The restaurants were well run and provided great service. We especially enjoyed the breakfast specials at the Chiefs Hut and the lunch buffet at Shorebirds. The staff of the hotel was friendly and willing to help out in any way they could. When our bags were brought up to the room by the bell staff I questioned him on the location of the ice machine. He took our ice bucket and filled it with ice for us (and pointed it out so we could find it later) There are timeshare people in the lobby but we politely said no thank you each time they asked us if we wanted to receive a free gift and they did not bother us at all. However, I will note there were alot of people lined up to talk to them so the business is obviously worth their efforts. In conclusion, we highly recommend this property...pay the extra money for the ocean view room it is well worth it and after all you can see city sights and other buildings from hotel rooms in your hometown, you can only see the beaches of Honolulu from an oceanview room in Hawaii!!!

<Author>knuckles01
<Content>A Great Hotel We cruised from Vancouver to Hawaii in Sept/Oct 2004, and before flying home, stayed 3 days at the Outrigger Reef on the Beach. The travel agent booked the hotel and said it was above average, but after reading some of the previous reviews on TripAdvisor, we became quite concerned.We disembarked the ship in Honolulu on Oct. 6 at about 11:00 am and took a taxi to the hotel. We realized it was a little early to check in, but hoped our room would be ready. It wasn't, and to our surprise, we were told it wouldn't be ready until 3:00 pm, which is later than most hotels in our experience. They did take our luggage though, so we were able to wander around Waikiki until 3:00.The room was ready exactly on time. We were on the 11th floor of the Pacific tower facing the beach, and had a standard room. It was a corner room (1163 or 1164 I believe) and we had a partial view of the ocean. The room was large, with a balcony, a king sized bed, a kitchenette, a couch, and a good sized kitchen table. It was certainly larger than most rooms I've had in hotels across Canada or the US. The only negative thing I noted about the room was that there was no bathtub, just a shower. Having just spent 11 days on a cruise ship with a tiny shower, my wife was looking forward to a bath. I prefer showers anyway, so wasn't bothered at all. It was a large shower, so I was quite comfortable.The hotel was beautiful, the service from the front desk, the concierge, the bell desk, the restaurants, and the shops in the hotel was first class. There was outstanding entertainment in the open lobby every day and they even provided exercise classes on the beach every morning at 7:00 am. I must say that I was disappointed with the beach; the sand outside the hotel and the adjoining park was more like silica than the powder found farther up Waikiki beach towards Diamond Head, and the beach was quite rocky in the water. One of the bell staff told me that the sand was trucked in when the area was developed. I should also note that I was very disappointed that the hotel provided space in the main lobby for a time-share sales company. They were moderately aggressive and because they were stationed between the elevators and the street, we were accosted at least a dozen times in the 3 days we were there. Overall, the hotel was beautiful. The room and the amenities were very good (except for the lack of a bathtub); the service from all staff was outstanding; but the time share harassment was quite annoying. The beach was not what we expected, but I believe the city was responsible for that, not the hotel. I would not hesitate to stay at the Outrigger Reef on the Beach again if I have the opportunity to return to Hawaii.
