<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Wonderful Place to spend our honeymoon My husband and I went to Oahu for our Honeymoon; we stayed 7 days at Reef on the Beach. September 20-28, 2004. We got to the hotel about 6pm, two steps out of the van and the bellhop was there with a cart to take our luggage. We checked in, room 600 in the Ocean Tower (the 2nd set of elevators). We go up to the room and open the door and there waiting for us is a bottle of champagne. We had an inside room, but if you went out on the porch you could still see the ocean which I was very excited about!We called Bell Services and they brought our bags up very quickly. During our stay we also acquired maintenance for our TV, we wanted to rent a movie and it wouldn't allow us. They came up and had a new box on the TV in 20 minutes or less and also house keeping, the blow dryer died on me, they had a new one for me in 5 minutes.The room was nice and clean, before we left I heard a lot of reviews about the small showers.... though it wasn't a huge bathroom but I didn't think the shower was that small. It was a stand up shower and served its purpose very well.The hotel has different crafters each day of the week in the lobby area, we loved going day each day and seeing the new craft that was there! Also check your info sheet for the hotel (under door every couple of days) they have morning exercises on the beach and shows and music and my husband and I also renewed our vows on the beach on Friday morning when we were there. It was wonderful and the hotel does this service for free, we said vows in Hawaiian and then our own personal vows and at the end we received a certificate.We went out for breakfast at the Chief's Hut almost everyday. They have morning specials for $4.95, service is friendly and quick and the food is very good.We also at Dinner at the Shorebird, this beach overlook the beach. With each dinner you get all you can eat salad bar, the salad bar is huge, I really didn't even need my chicken dinner after the salad bar! So we got up and got our salad bar and sat down, they brought our meat out to us... you cook your own dinner!! It was pretty neat!There is a starbucks in the lobby, which is very friendly and quick, and they were also building a smoothie company that is connected to starbucks, which should be open in late Oct/early Nov.The pool (salt water pool!) is very nice and as long as you get out there by 8am-9am you'll get your choice of lounge chairs. What we did was get a chair and then grab a bit to eat. The hot tubs are awesome so relaxing after a day of walking!The ocean, Waikiki is a man made beach and the water has a lot of big rocks in them... I didn't like swimming in the water, but the beach is a wonderful place to get a tan!The front desk gave us a small package when we checked in, we were giving 3 postcards from the outrigger... we were told we didn't have to put stamps on them just give them back to the front desk... to date the 3 postcards we sent out have yet to reach their destinations... I suggest keep those as a keepsake and buy then at any store for 7 for a buck and then stamps...We shopped in almost every shop there, they were all pleasant and nice and the prices aren't too high... 6 t-shirts for $20 downstairs! Though you can get 8 for $20 if you walk down to International MarketWe did do the time-share, I would recommend it... I did it for the $100 gift cert we got... they estimate 90-120 minutes we were there for 2 1/2 hours and they really try to sell the time share to us... but my husband finally told them no and we got our $100 and left. They did ask a few times if we had gone to their presentation but really there were only 4 or 5 people who work there and they started recognizing us after a day or two... All in all we had a wonderful time and we would go back again and again if we have the chance.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A high-low hotel We stayed here in 2000 in a partial ocean view room. The location is wonderful, the beach is right out the back door, the water is close to the hotel (useful to know for handicapped travellers) and all the staff were friendly, efficient and professional. The services we used were good quality, the pool was a little crowded (but that seem standard for Waikiki) but clean, and we were able to use it when we wanted. The hotel is not the best for middle-of-the-road travellers -- you should either pay for the good views or choose the cheap rooms, and dine at the oceanfront restaurants or off property. Our room had a wonderful view of the hotel next door, and if we went out on the lanai to see a sliver of ocean, we were serenaded by the air conditioners. We probably should have asked for a higher floor or an upgrade (and we may next time) but that was our only real disappointment. I was unimpressed with the quality of the Chief's Hut, but the other restaurants were satisfactory.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Not perfect, but excellent We recently returned from a week's stay in Oahu for our honeymoon. When I chose the Outrigger Reef, I had read all the reviews and knew what to expect. Yes, the bathrooms are tiny. Yes, there are nicer hotels. But I'll tell you this - I highly doubt there is a better hotel in Honolulu for the money.We stayed in an ocean front room - probably one of the best views from a hotel lanai in Honolulu (the hotel sits on the beach, about 30 feet away from the water). The room came with a king bed, a couch, two chairs and a table, plus chairs and a small table on the lanai. The room itself was not overly spectacular, but if you plan to spend most of your time in your hotel room, you probably shouldn't be going to Hawaii!The beach in front of the hotel - which is NOT Waikiki, as other reviewers have mistakenly stated - doesn't get too crowded (like Waikiki), but there are better beaches on the island to relax at (try the North Shore). It really empties out when the sun goes down, which gives you a chance to take a nice, quiet beach stroll or to sit on your lanai and listen to the ocean.As stated by other reviewers, the staff is very friendly. The timeshare people can be annoying, but easily avoided. The valets work hard at their jobs, but occasionally it can take a while to get your car (when there's only three of them trying to get cars for a lobby full of people, the long wait is understandable). The restaurants are good, but not great.Overall, if you're going to Oahu to try and take in as much as the island has to offer, this is a great place to stay. A lot of things are within walking distance, and it's a nice place to return to after a day on the beach or seeing the sites. If you plan to spend most of your time in your room, I'd suggest staying somewhere else.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Absolutely perfect We spent a week of our honeymoon here and the hotel was faultless. Spotlessly clean at all times, the staff were all friendly and welcoming. Nothing was too much trouble for them.There's a good selection of shops on the premises, selling clothing, food and drink and a whole lot more, and three restaurants. Our favourite was The Shore Bird, overlooking Waikiki Beach, where you're given raw pieces of meat or fish to take over and cook yourself on their barbecue. Rooms were compact but very functional, with a safe and fridge in the room, although the bathroom was a little small. The lifts are very slow, but then again, this is Hawaii! We concluded that the lifts ran on Hawaiian time!The hotel is in a good location, between the market place area to the east and the Ala Moana shopping area to the west. I'd stay at the Outrigger Reef again in a heartbeat and can recommend it to anybody.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Don't hesitate.....stay here! After booking, then reading the reviews we tried to find another hotel. We couldn't because their was a big convention in town. We stayed the last week in July. I loved this hotel! We had booked a city view room for the price, but were upgraded to a partial ocean view overlooking the ocean and the pool. Room was terrific. We kept the lanai (sp.?) doors open the entire time we were in the room even at night. The only negative thing was there was only a shower no bathtub. Bathroom was more than okay. Things to think about:We were told everything was sooo expensive. Not so. Stay away from expensive places. We mostly ate what the locals ate and for great prices. The bakery in the bottom of the hotel across the street was wonderful. You can eat till your stuffed for under $3. Lunch plates could be found everywhere for under $6. Zippy's fast food restaurent was local, cheap, and great. If you want a truly memorable meal and have an extra $100 try The Ocean House in the hotel and eat sitting by the beach. You will not be sorry. Drinks are expensive most places. Across the street at the Broilerhouse, Mai-Tai's are under $2, though. if you have a car, Kailua and Lanikae (sp.?) are beautiful places to go swim and not crowded. Buzz' Steakhouse is another memorable, but expensive place to eat across from Kailua Beach. Go at lunch. You really should have a reservation for dinner if you don't want to wait. Try the Artichoke for an appetizer and the Key Lime Pie with Guava Sauce for dessert. Terrific!! We did lots of touristy things, but the one you don't want to miss out on is the Polynesian Culteral Center. Definitely worth the time. If I could only do one thing, (besides the beaches) that would be it. The hotel beach was fine, but the sand in the water was rocky. You can walk two minutes in either direction and the water is fine. We spent time and thoroughly enjoyed the beach around the hotel. It wasn't that crowded except for Saturday and Sunday. Other beaches around the island were more private and the sand was of a better quality. Other things not to miss are the Internatial Market Bazaar. Cheap gifts. For even cheaper gifts (but the sme ones) try the Swap Meet at the Aloha Stadium. Good quality t-shirts $2 are everywhere. You might want to buy a BIG quality rolling suitcase to take back all your stuff in for only $10! Whatever you wanted to take back you could fin it at the Staium. All in all we had a great vacation! About the hotel, it was a great place to come back to. One hint. Ask for the highest floor possible. We were on the 16th out of 17. It's easier to catch an elevator that's empty and not have to try to push your way into a crowded one.

They run out early - I got one of the last spots at 10 a.m. and the staff said you should get there by 9 to guarantee a spot. With the umbrellas and chairs, there was no room for people who just want to lay down a towel and sunbathe (for free).Its understandable because its a huge city and there are lots of tourists - and it is one of just a few hotels in Waikiki that are directly on the beach. They are probably all crowded. They have good food and drinks and good bands playing at night (on the weekends).Another positive was that it is centrally located. It was an easy walk to many great restaurants and shops. It is definitely a vibrant, fun city.We got the room at the Outrigger for a good price through Hotels.com. However, I feel that I wouldn't do that again because I suspect that is why we were stuck in the terrible room (we paid rock bottom prices). Overall the hotel is busy, which was not what I was looking for, but is attractive. Despite my experience, I think its a good value, especially if you just plan to use it as a base to explore Oahu.

<Content>Will try a different hotel next time My fiance' and I just got back from Hawaii a few days ago. The Outrigger Waikiki is very misleading on the room sizes on their web page. I have never seen a bathroom so small in my life. The Outrigger Reef has a special promotion that gives you a free catamaran sail if you stay five nights or longer, which we did. Before our trip, I contacted the hotel to inquire about this, as we should have been eligible. The staff at that time assured me that it would be no problem at all, we would get our free sail info at check in. But when we got there, we were told we couldn't get that either. To save expenses on the trip, we purchased a phone card to make long distance calls-I discovered 3 days into our trip that, even with a phone card, there is a 97 cent charge whenever you pick up the phone to dial a number, phone card or not. The rooms all have balconies, which is wonderful; none of the balconies has an available screen, so you could never keep the patio doors open, because insects could get in. Another tip: If you want your hotel room cleaned early, leave a tip and a small note for housekeeping. Our first day there, our room wasn't cleaned until after 3p.m., but after we left a tip, (which we didn't mind doing) we quickly moved up the food chain, and our room was the 1st one done each day. The timeshare people were a total nightmare. The are like the perfume sprayers at the malls, but 10 times worse. They nearly tackle you as they fast talk you to get your credit card number to sign you up for a pressure breakfast to get you to buy into a time share. No matter how many times you tell them you're not interested, it never ends. We were approached by them at least 30 times in the 6 days we were there. It can be extremely overwhelming. Please shop around for souvenirs; the hotel store is very overpriced. It is on the beach, but be prepared to pay for additional items like umbrella and chair rentals.The hotel is beautiful and spacious, and it was our 1st trip to Hawaii, but we've already decided that when we go back next year, it will be to a different hotel.

<Rating>4	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	

<Author>Imaginaryfriend3
<Content>Xtra tips inside, Good  I stayed at the Reef back in May 2003 and thought it was a great hotel to stay at. It's not located at the prime Waikiki spot but you can take the Bus or walk down to other beach spots. It's location is great if you plan to go nightclubbing where the locals go, see nightlife section below for highlights. I took the Bus to the nightclubs and then took a Taxi home (the bus system stops running at 11 or 12) having them drop me off at the nearby bus stop (50 yards from hotel entrance) since the hotel is on a 1-way street and it would cost you $5 more for a direct hotel drop-off. Get your Bus 4 consecutive day pass for $15 at any ABC store, also get the Map guide from them for around $3-$5 bucks. Forget those bus tours, use Hawaii's bus system (thebus.org) and see the sites on your own schedule.Food! ---------------------------------- Pick up those coupon bookets like This week Oahu and save lots of money on meals. Also do the early bird specials that alot of restaurants offer. One few of my favorite places to eat were Davey Jones Ribs (early bird special of either the ribs or the galic chicken legs) and the Lanai loft (get the local plate of Mahi Mahi, use coupon in booklets to get free drink).Nightlife spots that don't suck! ----------------------------------------------------- 1. Ocean Club ... located in Restaurant row - Tuesdays and Thursdays, Saturday, 21and older, good food (pupus) get there before 8pm for 1/2 price pupus. Tuesday night gets a happy hour crowd, Thursday's are packed. Weekends are also good. 2. Compadres at the Ward Center - Wednesday nights 3. Pipeline Cafe ... located on a side street near the Ward Shopping center - Friday  Saturday, 18 and over crowd. Didn't see a weekday crowd but probably more of a weekend spot. 4. Rumors ... located in the Ala Moana Shopping center - Friday  Saturday, older crowd

<Rating>4	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice hotel - a good time Stayed here in the first week of August as part of our honeymoon. After reading so many reviews talking of upgrades we were hoping that we'd be helped out what with it being our honeymoon. The receptionist showed no emotion or congratulations and just offered us an upgrade if we payed $210 (partial ocean view) or $350 (ocean view) for our 7 night stay......... thanks very much. We decided to go for an ocean view to be told that it was a smoking room. We therefore dumped this idea and settled for paying an extra $210 to have a partial ocean view. Our room was high up in the hotel which meant we had a nice view of the pool and could see the ocean - can't complain there. In the room we had a king size bed, a sofabed and a table and chairs. Also had a refigerator and a microwave, and in the bathroom (decent size) there was a shower only.As it was our honeymoon we got a note through the door saying that we could get two glasses of champagne in the bar, and we were left a present which was a small wooden bowl with two cookies and some nuts (weird). Mind you, as we'd paid them an extra $210 to upgrade our room it was the very very least we could expect.The hotel itself is very nice and we found it to be clean and the staff fairly courteous. The decor wasn't the freshest but I suppose you can't renovate every single year. Our favourite restaurant was the Shorebird which looked right out onto the beach and ocean. Nice bar to sit at with a lovely view, and nice food. In the evening you choose your meat and cook it yourself on the grill - something to make it more enjoyable but it was very very hot at the grillside!As for the beach, it was lovely and you can reserve two beds and an umbrella for $30 a day. The sea is shallow for a long way, but there are some rocks which can hurt so tread carefully.The pool is nice but can sometimes get crowded with children. There are plenty of beds around the pool but if you're a sun worshipper get one at the far side of the pool (by the whirlpool) as this is where the sun shines for most of the day - most of the morning and all afternoon.Waikiki itself is a bustling resort and never seems to sleep. However at night some of the side roads leading to the hotel are very dark and can seem a bit scary to non-locals.Overall a very nice hotel, not far off being fairly close to perfection. A few more touches would make it perfect. Would we stay there again? Possibly, but I might be tempted to go for one of the more upmarket ones next time.

<Rating>4	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Location, Great Property My wife and I stayed 7 nights at Outrigger Reef, Room 518, July 11-18, 2003. We booked the rooms through Northwest (Airlines) Vacations and MLT Vacations as part of as air/lodging/car rental package. We paid for a non-smoking, partial-ocean room and upon check-in, with a brief suggestion by my wife, were upgraded to an ocean-view room. This was our first trip to Hawaii that also included 3 days on the big Island at Outrigger Kanaloa at Kona.From the lanai (two chairs and a tiny table), we watched surfers every morning as well as the sun rising over Diamond Head. The room, except for the bathroom, was spatious. There was a king bed (firm), a sofa/hide-a-bed, and a small table with two chairs. The room also had a television, refridgerator, coffee maker, iron and ironing board, six feet or more of closet space (with hangers) and a safe. Coffee packets were replaced daily, and the safe cost $3 per day when we used it.The small but adequate bathroom had a tub/shower combo (excellent shower, slow but adequate drainage in the tub) and one sink with a bit of counter space. Opposite the sink there was another small counter and a mirror. The odd placement of the toilet made it rather cumbersome to open and close the bathroom door. The room, including its fixtures, accessories, and so on, were in good repair. Daily maid service met our expectations.We came to Hawaii for a meeting my wife attended and traveled with another couple. That couple had reserved an Outrigger Reef Run of the House room that turned out to be much smaller than ours, including a shower only, no space for couch/hide-a-bed, and a view of an exterior wall of the hotel. Craning their necks around the corner of their lanai, they could catch a glimpse of the pool. They sought an upgrade but were offered only a room that was adjacent to the elevator, which they declined.Outrigger Reef has beach access directly behind the hotel. In fact, we virtually stepped from the hotel onto the beach. The beach runs the width of the hotel property (and beyond the property, of course). During most of the day (before 10 am through mid to late afternoon), the narrow beach is filled with guests using umbrellas and chairs provided by the hotel (at a cost, I assume). The ocean water is shallow for a long way out, but there are enough rocks on the beach floor here to make it uncomfortable or at least a nusiance for some.The good-sized pool within the hotel was always in use. There is an adjacent whirlpool, as well as another pair of whirlpools several feet and a few stair steps away from the pool. The hotel provides beach and pool towels, at no cost, simply by asking and signing for them at a desk near the pool.There is a restaurant adjacent to the swimming pool (we ate there once, it was fine) and two restaurants adjacent to the beach. We ate the buffet breakfast at the less-formal beach-side restaurant. There was quite a variety of items, including lots of fresh fruit. The service was fine.We had a rental car and parked it in the hotel's valet parking. All the attendents were friendly and efficient and came to recognize us after a couple days. Parking costs $11 per day.There are lots of retail shops within the Outrigger Reef property. We used The Pantry for breakfast items (milk, juice, cereal) as well as for snacks and beach mats. The ABC store, just up the block on Beachwalk Road, provides lots of those types of items as well. There is a timeshare desk within the property (where isn't there a timeshare desk in Hawaii?) that offers a very handy and useful O'ahu/Waikiki map. Listen to their initial 3-minute intro and the laminated tri-fold map is yours!Outrigger Reef is close to lots of shopping, restaurants, and Waikiki attractions. Honolulu and, specifically, the Waikiki area, are densely populated with people and cars. The sooner you get comfortable with that, the better stay you'll have. Allow lots of time to get places and walk whenever you can.We very much enjoyed our first stay in Hawaii at the Outrigger Reef and would happily return there. All the staff were friendly and relaxed. They made us feel appreciated as hotel guests.When we go to Hawaii the next time, we'll likely again pay for the comfort and view of an upgraded room. Much of that decision, however, depends on one's budget, one's plans, and one's expectations. Will you want to spend significant daylight hours in your room, or is it only for sleeping? What do you want to see from your lanai every morning or each night? Invest time well before you book your trip to adress these and similar questions, especially if it's your first trip. We learned a lot and will be better prepared and have more realistic expectations when we go again, and we will go again!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Hotel Great, Room Terrible Went for a 3 island honeymoon in Oct. 2000 that began in Oahu. After the 12 hour plane ride, we were looking for some rest and relaxation. Of course, driving into Waikiki sets you off right off the bat. Our partial ocean view room was hardly what we were expecting. Unless the building 20 feet from our window was the ocean, this definition meant that if we stuck our video camera out the window the 4 inches that it opened and turned it to the left, we could get video of the ocean and then replay it for our viewing pleasure. The room was cramped and malodorous and the shower door didn't open all the way without hitting the toilet.. nice walk-in closet though.. weird use of space. Then we went to the pool for a dip in the hot tub after our long trip and after about 15 min, we got kicked out, told the pool closed at 10 pm. I don't know, I've stayed at a lot of hotels and one of the best perks of an outdoor pool is coming back after a long day of sight seeing and taking a late night dip in the pool. Other than that, the hotel itself was very, very nice. Beautiful breakfast location at the Shore Bird and great fresh fruit. And the hotel is right on the beach at Waikiki, so if you are never planning to be in your room, this is the place. We are going back in August and we were going to stay there again, but this time with an Ocean Front room, because we did like the hotel itself, but then we realized that the cost is so outrageous, there are many other better hotels to choose from in that price range.

<Content>Excellent beachfront value in crowded Waikiki Even without its jaw-dropping views of Diamond Head and the ocean, my decent-sized room, with a small but efficiently designed shower-only bathroom, would be a good value in this prime location right on the sand. Pool is rather dark and not ideally located, though the nice beach is right next to Fort DeRussy park. Overall, the Reef is great for a lively vacation in an ideal spot, perhaps the best value on Waikiki beach.
